Current Commentary

On the Unfortunate Incident in Chengdu

— Yi

All people who love peace in both China and Japan feel deeply regret for the Chengdu incident that occurred on the 24th of this month, because this incident has given a great stimulus to national sentiment, and the development of this stimulus may be harmful to the peace of East Asia.

We are still unable to fully understand the root cause of this unfortunate incident, but the following two conclusions can be drawn simply from the various news that is already known:

First, among those who sacrificed their lives in this unexpected incident, in addition to our country's people and military police, were Watanabe, a reporter for the Osaka Mainichi Shimbun, and Fukagawa, a reporter for the Shanghai Mainichi Shimbun. Both Japanese reporters were dispatched by their newspapers to serve as correspondents. This time, they were killed by rioters for no reason in the interior of our country. In any case, the rational people in our country cannot help but feel deep sympathy. From the perspective of a great nation, we should cherish any foreigner who engages in a peaceful occupation as much as our own compatriots. Therefore, we not only mourn from the bottom of our hearts for the two Japanese who were engaged in peaceful work, but after this incident, we have become more aware of the importance of promoting the spirit of universal love and the danger of shallow nationalists shooting indiscriminately in mass movements.

Second, the administrative authorities of the central government and various provinces have done their best in recent years to protect foreign nationals, especially Japanese nationals. The increase in the number of Japanese nationals in our country and the strong sales of Japanese goods in recent years are obvious evidence. However, unexpected violent incidents cannot be avoided even in politically clear Japan, let alone in our country, which is deeply burdened by national disasters. The occurrence of the Chengdu incident can be said to be due to the local authorities' negligence in prevention, but analyzing the excessive emotions of the rioters, it is indeed somewhat due to the evil consequences planted by Japanese soldiers in the past five years. From this point of view, it is clear that only by adjusting Sino-Japanese relations on the condition of absolutely respecting our country's independence and sovereignty can similar unfortunate incidents be prevented from happening again in the future.

We hope that those in China and Japan who truly want to maintain peace in East Asia will use calm reason to consider this unfortunate incident.

Chengdu Incident: China and Japan Send Personnel to Investigate; Japanese Consul in Chongqing Ordered to Fly to Chengdu; Ministry of Foreign Affairs Also Sends Commissioners; Military Police Closely Protect Japanese Nationals

(Nanjing) In order to understand the truth about the Chengdu incident, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs sent Commissioners Yang Kaijia and Section Chief Shao Yulin to investigate. Yang and Shao flew directly to Chengdu on the China Aviation Corporation Douglas 24 aircraft at 8 a.m. on the 28th. Matsumura, a third secretary from the Japanese Embassy who was sent to investigate the truth, also flew to Chengdu via Nanjing on the 28th. Wu Zexiang, Special Commissioner of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Sichuan and Kangding, telegraphed Nanjing on the 28th to report on the investigation and handling process. As for the aftermath of the deceased Japanese, China and Japan are handling it together. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Hankou) Ministry of Foreign Affairs Commissioners Yang Kaijia and Section Chief Shao Yulin flew from Nanjing to Chongqing and then to Chengdu via Hankou on the Nanjing postal plane at 10:30 a.m. on the 28th to investigate the truth of the Chengdu incident. Accompanying them were two reporters, Nakamura, a Shanghai-based correspondent for the Asahi Shimbun, and others. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Nanjing) According to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Special Commissioner Wu Zexiang of Sichuan and Kangding telegraphed the ministry on the 28th, reporting that in addition to sending condolences to the families of the two Japanese reporters who were killed, the injured were treated by the local government, and the truth of the civil unrest and riots will be investigated by the military and political authorities. In the meantime, military police will closely protect Japanese nationals. Both China and Japan are currently sending personnel to investigate the truth. It is expected that after the investigation, both sides will only deal with it as a disturbance by local rioters and will not affect Sino-Japanese relations because of this, so the situation will not escalate. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Chengdu) Six people, Matsumura, Secretary of the Japanese Embassy, ​​Kenji Kasuya, Japanese Consul in Chongqing, Masago Nakamura of the Osaka Asahi Shanghai Branch, Shinryo Tachibana of the Osaka Mainichi Shanghai Branch, Fusao Okamoto of the Domei News Agency Hankou Branch, and Takahiro Nitta of the South Manchuria Railway Hankou Branch, arrived in Chengdu on the afternoon of the 28th by Eurasia China Aviation large aircraft from Shanghai and Chongqing, respectively. The provincial government sent personnel to take care of them properly, and the route from the airport to the guesthouse was heavily guarded. Kasuya visited Wu Zexiang. At 7 p.m., Matsumura, Kasuya, and the Japanese reporters who arrived in Chengdu, as well as Shibo and Japanese doctors, accompanied by Wu Zexiang, Fan Chongze, and others, went to Zhenggu Street to inspect the bodies of the two deceased Japanese reporters, Watanabe and Fukagawa. At 8 p.m., they went to the military medical office of the governor's office to comfort the injured Takeo Tanaka and Naoshi Seto and inquired in detail about the Chengdu riot. It ended at 9 p.m. More than a dozen members of the Chengdu press visited Nakamura and others after they arrived in Chengdu in their capacity as colleagues, talked briefly, and then left. Ministry of Foreign Affairs Section Chief Shao Yulin flew to Chengdu from Nanjing by plane at 5 p.m. on the 28th to investigate the Chengdu case. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Chongqing) Ministry of Foreign Affairs Commissioners Yang Kaijia and Section Chief Shao Yulin flew to Chongqing from Nanjing on the afternoon of the 28th. Yang deplaned in Chongqing and is scheduled to fly to Chengdu on the 29th. Shao flew directly to Chengdu on the original plane to investigate the riot incident. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Hankou) Nitta and Okamoto flew from Hankou to Sichuan on the 27th to investigate the Chengdu incident. Several others continued to fly there by plane on the 28th. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Chongqing) On the 28th, Japanese Consul Kenji Kasuya of Chongqing flew to Chengdu with four attendants to investigate the truth of the Chengdu case. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Chongqing) Consul Kasuya, under the orders of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, is scheduled to fly to Chengdu at 3 p.m. on the 28th to jointly investigate the details of the incident with the Chinese authorities. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Nanjing) Regarding the Chengdu riots affecting Japanese nationals, both China and Japan are now sending personnel to investigate the truth. Lu Zuofu, Director of the Sichuan Construction Department, arrived in Nanjing from Sichuan on the morning of the 28th. In addition to contacting the issuance of Sichuan construction bonds to repay old debts, he also took the opportunity to visit Foreign Minister Zhang at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at about 10 a.m. on the 28th to report on the details of the Chengdu riots. It is reported that Lu will return to Sichuan after his business in Nanjing is completed. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

After the Japanese Regular Cabinet Meeting, the Three Ministers Confer on Countermeasures; The Matter Should be Handled by Both Governments; Investigate the Cause and Fundamentally Resolve

(Tokyo) The regular cabinet meeting on the 28th was held at the Prime Minister's residence at 9:30 a.m. At the outset, Foreign Minister Arita reported on the Chengdu incident in detail and presented the intentions of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which meant that since a specific report had not yet been received from Consul General Suma in Nanjing, countermeasures for the future could not be clearly decided. The meeting adjourned at 11 a.m. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Tokyo) Japanese Foreign Minister Arita, Minister of War Terauchi, and Minister of the Navy Nagano continued to hold a three-minister meeting at the Prime Minister's residence after the regular cabinet meeting adjourned this morning. First, Foreign Minister Arita reported on the Chengdu incident and the illegal border crossing and shooting incident on the Soviet-Manchu border. Then, they began important discussions. Concrete measures for the Chengdu incident will be discussed and decided. Once Ambassador Kawagoe returns to Shanghai tomorrow, based on the detailed report of the incident from Consul General Suma in Nanjing and the protest process, he will submit a formal report to the Foreign Minister, and then instruct the ambassador to comply. (China United Press dispatch, 28th)

(Tokyo) Japanese Foreign Minister Arita, Minister of War Terauchi, and Minister of the Navy Nagano stayed at the Prime Minister's residence after the cabinet meeting on the 28th and held a three-minister meeting from 11:30 a.m. Foreign Minister Arita explained the Chengdu incident in more detail, and then exchanged views on the recent problem of illegal Soviet border crossings in the eastern border area of ​​the Soviet Union and Manchuria. The meeting ended at noon. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Tokyo) Today, a spokesman for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs claimed that Japanese personnel had already gone to Chengdu to investigate the case. The Japanese government has not yet decided on its attitude before receiving the report. In addition to resolving the case, the Chinese and Japanese authorities should also find ways to prevent such cases from happening again in the future. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

(Tokyo) Japanese Foreign Minister Arita made a concluding report on the Chengdu incident at today's cabinet meeting, stating that countermeasures for the Chengdu incident must be decided after receiving accurate and complete information from local investigators. Arita believes that in addition to the usual demands for punishing murderers and compensating for losses, it is necessary to take fundamental steps. The cabinet then followed Arita's conclusion and decided to leave the decision of the steps to the three ministers. After the cabinet meeting adjourned, the three ministers of Foreign Affairs, War, and Navy continued to meet. Arita immediately expressed his opinion, saying that the Chengdu incident should not be regarded as a local problem, but should be handled by the governments of China and Japan. The authorities of the two countries should investigate the cause and fundamentally resolve it. Afterwards, a thorough discussion was held on the specific plans and active actions to adjust Sino-Japanese relations, which lasted for an hour. A spokesman for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs told foreign news reporters this afternoon that since the Chengdu incident, China has been filled with anti-Japanese sentiment, like a gas that is easily ignited and can explode once ignited. Therefore, Japan's most urgent need is to eliminate this gas. The Chinese and Japanese authorities should urgently consider the proper methods to implement this urgent task. When asked whether the Sino-Japanese incident was caused by the recent anti-Japanese sentiment prevalent among the Chinese or the result of Chinese dissatisfaction with Japan, the spokesman hesitated and replied that he did not know. Looking at the general situation, most newspapers described the Chengdu incident with stimulating and indignant words, and all parties hoped that the incident would be resolved quickly so that the future negotiations between China and Japan would not be hampered. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

Injured Japanese Nationals Gradually Recover; Seto Details the Course of the Riot; Tanaka Issues a Written Statement

(Chengdu) Three people, including Shibo Kakuro, a member of the Japanese Consulate in Chongqing, and a Japanese doctor, flew to Chengdu from Chongqing on the 26th. In the evening, they went to the military hospital of the governor's office to visit the Japanese nationals Takeo Tanaka and Naoshi Seto, who were injured in the Chengdu riot on the 24th. According to Shibo, who spoke to a news reporter who visited him at 11 a.m. on the 27th, after we arrived in Chengdu, we went to comfort our injured compatriots, Takeo Tanaka and Naoshi Seto. Tanaka's injuries were minor and he has gradually recovered. Seto's head is slightly feverish, and he will recover if he rests again. Tanaka can already write with a pen, and Seto is in good spirits. He can still remember the details of the unfortunate incident and described the situation at that time in a loud voice. He said that at 3 p.m. on the 24th, someone came to the Da Chuan Hotel to inquire about their mission in Chengdu. They replied that they were merchants and news reporters, and that they were all traveling for leisure and had nothing to do with the establishment of a consulate. After hearing this answer, everyone left without any other changes. Seto also said that at about 5 p.m., when they were resting on the second floor of the hotel, suddenly tens of thousands of people gathered inside and outside the Da Chuan Hotel, and the noise was deafening. Then they heard the sound of windows and glass breaking, and they knew that the Da Chuan Hotel had been destroyed by rioters. At that time, the military police stationed at the Da Chuan Hotel to protect them were weak and unable to stop the rioters. The military police escorted the four of them to the third floor for protection. Not long after they went upstairs, the rioters swarmed to the third floor and destroyed all the items in the building, causing great chaos. Seto continued to say that in this chaotic situation, they were pushed out of the hotel by the rioters and bumped around in the crowd on the street. The rioters gathered more and more people, and the four of them and the protecting military police were dispersed and unable to take care of each other. Seto concluded that after this disturbance, his nerves were dizzy, and later he learned that he was escorted to the hospital by the police. According to Tanaka, after being dispersed, when he was unable to escape from the crowd, he was suddenly held by a stout gentleman, and he struggled to escape. Later, he learned that this gentleman was the director of the Public Security Bureau. He expressed his gratitude for Fan's efforts to save his life. The bodies of the two deceased Japanese, Watanabe and Fukagawa, have been inspected by personnel from the Japanese Embassy and the Japanese Consul, and it has now been decided to cremate them in Chengdu. The two injured Japanese have requested to fly to Shanghai on the morning of the 29th, but have not yet been granted permission by the doctor, as they are afraid that they will not be able to withstand the long journey, which may affect their injuries. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Chongqing) Tanaka, an employee of the South Manchuria Railway Company who survived the attack by rioters, was found to be in serious condition after the investigation, and he is still not out of danger. Although Seto's injuries were serious, fortunately, he did not suffer any vital injuries, and his life can be saved. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Chengdu) Takeo Tanaka, a Japanese national injured in the Chengdu case, gave a written statement to the Central News Agency reporter in Japanese on the 28th, describing the details of the Chengdu case, which is very detailed. The following is a summary of a few points: (1) During the disturbance, he showed his passport, and someone immediately stood up to speak. This speech was successful, and the crowd withdrew. (2) When the crowd attacked for the second time, the room was dark, and several members of the Public Security Bureau protected us and worked hard to defend us, but they were unable to succeed due to the disparity in numbers. (3) We were dragged into the street by the crowd, and we were grateful to Director Fan for stopping the crowd, so that my life could be saved. I express my gratitude for Director Fan's efforts. After the bodies of the two deceased Japanese, Watanabe and Fukagawa, were inspected by personnel from the Japanese Embassy and the Japanese Consul, it has now been decided to cremate them in Chengdu. The two injured Japanese have requested to fly to Shanghai on the morning of the 29th, but have not yet been granted permission by the doctor, as they are afraid that they will not be able to withstand the long journey, which may affect their injuries. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

The central military authorities have been holding important meetings in Huangpu for days. After Summer Recess, Legislative Yuan's Regular Meeting Resumes Yesterday; Passes the Sichuan Construction and Old Debt Exchange Public Bond Regulations

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held its 69th meeting on the morning of the 28th, with 50 members including Chuan Bingchang attending. Sun Ke chaired, and Liang Hancao was the secretary-general. The "Regulations for the Sichuan Provincial Construction and Old Debt Exchange Public Bonds of the Republic of China Year 25" were passed. During the initial review of the regulations, Chen Changheng gave a detailed report on the purpose of issuing the public bonds, stating that the Sichuan Provincial Government originally planned to issue 45 million yuan of construction public bonds, and the central government approved the issuance of 30 million yuan first, and the rest would be issued when necessary. In addition to handling transportation and production construction projects, the public bonds must also be used to exchange old debts to balance income and expenditure, so the title of the regulations was changed to "Construction and Old Debt Exchange Public Bonds" to conform to the facts of 30 million yuan. According to Liu Hangchen, the director of the Sichuan Department of Finance, the detailed purpose is to allocate as follows: (1) 13 million yuan for transportation projects, including 8.5 million yuan for building the Chengdu-Chongqing section of the Sichuan-Han Railway and 4.5 million yuan for building the Sichuan-Yunnan and other highways; (2) 7 million yuan for production construction, including 2.5 million yuan for the share capital of the rural cooperative treasury, 250,000 yuan for the opening expenses of a vegetable oil factory to improve tung oil production, 500,000 yuan for silk industry improvement expenses, 1.75 million yuan for sugar industry improvement expenses, 1 million yuan for paper mill opening expenses, 300,000 yuan for alkali factory opening expenses, and 700,000 yuan for the opening expenses of three hydropower plants; (3) 10 million yuan for exchanging old debts. In the past, the Sichuan Provincial Government had borrowed more than 10 million yuan from the business community for bandit suppression and military needs during emergencies and had given short-term loan certificates with a tax rate of 1%. Now, exchanging the debts with public bonds can not only consolidate the credit of the loans but also reduce the burden on the provincial treasury because the interest rate is changed to 6%. After the speech, the case was passed without objection. Also, this meeting was the first Yuan meeting after the summer vacation. The members had been apart for more than a month during the summer vacation, and they greeted each other when they arrived at the meeting, and the situation was extremely harmonious. (28th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan passed the Regulations for the Sichuan Provincial Construction and Old Debt Exchange Public Bonds of the Republic of China Year 25 at a meeting on the 28th. The full text is as follows:

Article 1. The Sichuan Provincial Government issues public bonds in order to handle transportation and production construction projects and exchange old debts. The public bonds are named the "Sichuan Provincial Construction and Old Debt Exchange Public Bonds of the Republic of China Year 25." Article 2. The quota of this public bond is 30 million yuan in national currency, of which 20 million yuan is used for construction projects and 10 million yuan is used for exchanging old debts. Article 3. This public bond is scheduled to be issued on September 1, 1936. Article 4. The interest rate of this public bond is set at 6% per annum, and interest is paid twice a year at the end of February and the end of August each year. Article 5. The principal repayment period of this public bond is set at 15 years. Only interest is paid in the first year, and principal repayment starts from the end of February in 1938. Principal is repaid once every half year thereafter. The first to eighth repayments each repay 2% of the total amount, the ninth to sixteenth repayments each repay 3%, the seventeenth to twentieth repayments each repay 4%, the twenty-first to twenty-fourth repayments each repay 5%, and the twenty-fifth to twenty-eighth repayments each repay 6%, until the end of August in the 40th year of the Republic of China, when all principal and interest will be repaid. Each principal repayment is drawn by lot in Chongqing one month before the due date, and personnel from the Ministry of Finance and the Audit Department are dispatched to supervise. Article 6. The principal and interest repayment fund for this public bond is designated to be allocated from the Sichuan Provincial land tax revenue. The Sichuan Provincial Government shall order the Department of Finance to allocate the amount of principal and interest due each period according to the principal and interest repayment schedule to the Chongqing Branch of the Central Bank on a monthly average basis, and deposit it in the public bond fund account for special storage and preparation for payment. The Sichuan Post-Disaster Public Bond Fund Management Committee of the Republic of China Year 24 is designated to concurrently handle the fund management of this public bond. Article 7. The face value of this public bond is divided into four types: 10,000 yuan, 1,000 yuan, 100 yuan, and 10 yuan, all of which are in bearer form. Article 8. The Central Bank Chongqing Branch and the banks entrusted by the Central Bank are designated as the principal and interest repayment agencies for this public bond. Article 9. This public bond bond can be freely bought and sold and mortgaged. When security deposits must be paid in provincial official affairs, it can be used as a substitute. The winning lottery tickets and due coupons can also be used to pay all provincial taxes. Article 10. Those who forge this public bond or damage its credit shall be punished by the judicial organs according to law. Article 11. This regulation shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. (28th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Full Text of the New Treaty Published: Anglo-Egyptian Alliance Formed; Military Mutual Assistance to Deal with the Mediterranean Situation; New Treaty Valid for Twenty Years; Sudan Issue Still Not Satisfactorily Resolved

(London) The full text of the Anglo-Egyptian Treaty, signed in the historically famous Locarno Room of the Foreign Office on Wednesday, was published in a white paper today. The main purpose of the treaty is to end the British military occupation of Egypt and establish an alliance between the two countries. The British side must wait for the full discussion by the National Assembly before approving it, and the Egyptian side is expected to approve it in November.

After the treaty is initialed by the two countries and registered in Geneva, several events will occur, including Egypt's accession to the League of Nations. The United Kingdom has agreed to assist Egypt in achieving this goal.

The treaty has a total of sixteen articles, accompanied by (1) a detailed record of the interpretations agreed upon by both parties, (2) official documents exchanged on various matters, and (3) another agreement on the exemptions and special rights enjoyed by British troops in Egypt.

The effective period of the treaty is twenty years. After the expiration, if one party applies, both parties will negotiate and sign another treaty in light of the situation at that time to amend the various articles of the current treaty. However, after ten years have passed, if both parties are willing, they can negotiate to amend the current treaty at any time. Any amendment must stipulate that the alliance should continue in accordance with the principles contained in the current treaty.

Scope of Alliance: The treaty stipulates the scope of the alliance as follows:

(1) Neither party shall adopt an attitude or conclude a treaty that conflicts with the alliance. (2) If the United Kingdom and Egypt encounter any dispute with a third country that may lead to a break with that country, the two countries intend to consult to seek a peaceful resolution. (3) If the United Kingdom or Egypt engages in war, the other country will come out to assist it in the capacity of an alliance. All obligations are based on the Covenant of the League of Nations or the Paris Convention.

Military Mutual Assistance: The treaty pre-specifies the ways in which Egypt will assist as follows: In the event of an impending war, a threat of war, or a discernible international emergency, Egypt will provide the United Kingdom with all kinds of facilities within its power. This facility and this kind of assistance includes (1) the use of Egyptian ports, airfields, transportation, and all necessary administrative and legal plans, (2) the promulgation of martial law and the implementation of effective inspections, and (3) the convenience of dispatching British troops or reinforcements, etc.

Canal Defense: Regarding the protection of the Suez Canal, the treaty states that "The Suez Canal is an integral part of Egypt, but it is also a universal transportation route and a major transportation route for all parts of the British Empire. In order to cooperate with the Egyptian army to defend the canal, Egypt shall permit the United Kingdom to maintain an army of no more than 10,000 men and an air force of no more than 400 pilots in the canal area until the United Kingdom and Egypt mutually agree that the Egyptian army can, by its own means, surround the canal and ensure its proper and complete security. However, this garrison can be increased in times of war or threat of war and discernible international emergencies. At the expiration of the current treaty, the question of whether the Egyptian army is capable of ensuring the security of the canal shall be submitted to the Council of the League of Nations in accordance with the League of Nations Covenant implemented last month, or other persons or groups agreed upon by the United Kingdom and Egypt for arbitration if the two parties cannot agree. The Egyptian government agrees to build barracks in the canal area to house the British troops reaching the aforementioned number and to provide sufficient comfort and emergency water sources according to the needs of the British government. The Egyptian government also agrees to build roads, the most important of which is from the canal area across the Nile Delta to Alexandria, and from the canal area to Egyptian capital Cairo. The Egyptian authorities will also improve the railway facilities in the canal area. Once these works have been fully implemented to the satisfaction of both parties, all British troops stationed in Egypt, except those originally stationed in the canal, will be withdrawn to the canal area. This provision refers to the British troops in Cairo, Abassia and Hilmiyya, as well as the British troops stationed in Heliopolis, Shiroan, and Abu Qir, but the troops in the port of Alexandria are an exception and will retain their current status for a period of eight years, as both parties believe that the new barracks in the canal area will not be fully completed until then, and the improvement work on the roads and railways will not be completed until then.

Air Force Training: The new treaty also contains other military provisions as follows: (1) The British Air Force may fly anywhere with the permission of the Egyptian side for training, but the Egyptian Air Force may also fly freely over British territory to show reciprocal treatment. (2) In Egyptian territory and territorial waters, suitable landing sites and seaplane berthing facilities will be prepared for the use of the British Air Force. If the British authorities deem it necessary to add additional facilities, they must also do so. (3) Although the British personnel currently in the Egyptian army will be withdrawn, the Egyptian government should adopt the advice of the British military inspection team for the benefit of the alliance between the two parties so that the training of the Egyptian army and air force can be improved. (4) The British government will set up appropriate training institutions in its own country to allow Egypt to send its soldiers and others to receive new military training. (5) The armament equipment of the Egyptian army must be the same as that of the British army and must not be different from each other.

Extraterritoriality: The final section of the treaty contains clauses on the safety of foreigners, the status of foreign officials, and the surrender treaty on consular jurisdiction. The original text is as follows: "The British government recognizes that the Egyptian government is responsible for protecting the lives and property of foreigners traveling to Egypt, so the Egyptian government must faithfully fulfill this obligation. The police bureau in Egypt will be abolished immediately after the treaty is approved, but within the last five years, European personnel must still be retained in the police agencies of various cities in Egypt. During this period, the Egyptian police will still be led by British officers. The British government recognizes that, in accordance with the spirit of the times and the current situation in Egypt, various surrender provisions should no longer exist, so it intends to assist Egypt in contacting various countries that enjoy consular jurisdiction and other surrender rights so that they can negotiate an appropriate solution to each other on the following points: (1) Find a way to eliminate the restrictions on sovereignty when Egypt implements its legislative power. (2) Negotiate a transitional approach and stipulate an appropriate time limit, during which the Mixed Court will be temporarily retained. In addition to its original jurisdiction, it will also be granted the powers of the current consular court, and when this transitional period ends, the Mixed Court will be abolished. The legislation of the Egyptian government for foreigners must comply with the principles of modern law and must not discriminate against foreigners."

Accession to the League of Nations: The treaty also stipulates that the United Kingdom and Egypt will send ambassadors to each other, and the British government will assist Egypt in requesting to join the League of Nations as a member state. It also states that the rights and obligations of the United Kingdom and Egypt in the Covenant of the League of Nations and the Paris Convention are not affected by this article. If any objections arise regarding the implementation or interpretation of the various articles of this treaty that cannot be resolved through direct negotiations, they shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of the Charter of the League of Nations. (28th Reuters Dispatch)

British Newspapers' Editorials Celebrate, Deeming it a Victory for British Diplomacy

(London) This morning, most of the London morning newspapers published editorials expressing warm congratulations to those involved in the negotiation of the Anglo-Egyptian treaty. Only the Daily Mail and the Morning Post offered some criticism. The Times stated that the significance of this treaty is extremely clear and needs no further praise. For the past eighteen years, Britain and Egypt have coexisted in a state of unease, inequality, and instability. Now, this has transformed into a friendly alliance between two equal and independent sovereign states. We should naturally congratulate the two governments and their representatives for this diplomatic victory, it said. The Evening Standard commented that the satisfactory outcome of this treaty was quite beyond the expectations of most people. The speed and appropriateness with which the representatives of both countries negotiated this matter deserve celebration, it said. The Daily News believed that the public opinion of both countries could now put the unpleasant past behind them and would undoubtedly rejoice exceedingly, it said. The Daily Telegraph also stated that this treaty was nothing less than an alliance between two free nations, it said. However, the Daily Mail believed that this would strike a blow to the security of the entire Empire. The Morning Post also said, "Our worst fears have now been confirmed. The conclusion of this treaty is not the end of disputes between the two countries, but rather the beginning," it said. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

U.S. Secretary of War, Mr. Dern, Passes Away

(Washington) U.S. Secretary of War, Mr. Dern, aged sixty-four, had been ill for over a month. He passed away today at Walter Reed Hospital in Washington. Mr. Dern initially suffered from influenza. After being admitted to the hospital, he developed heart disease. Upon hearing the news, Washington officials immediately expressed their sorrow. All U.S. Army camps lowered their flags to half-mast in mourning. It was also decided to fire a salute every half hour tomorrow morning and, after the sounding of the retreat bugle in the evening, to fire a nineteen-gun salute in tribute. Until President Roosevelt appoints a new Secretary of War, the current Under Secretary, Mr. Woodring, will temporarily take charge of the department's affairs. The most promising candidates for the position are Governor McNutt of Indiana and former High Commissioner to the Philippines, Mr. Murphy. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

Bismarck, North Dakota U.S. President Roosevelt, who is currently traveling through drought-stricken areas, announced after hearing the news of Secretary of War Dern's death in Washington, "With Mr. Dern's passing, the American people have lost a loyal, talented, and honest public servant. The entire U.S. Army has lost a capable leader," he said. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

A Brief Biography of Mr. Dern The late U.S. Secretary of War, Mr. Dern, was born on September 8, 1872, in Dodge County, Nebraska, USA. After reaching adulthood, he entered the University of Nebraska. He was fond of sports and excelled at football. After graduating, he married Miss Blanc. They had seven children. Mr. Dern's parents, driven by financial hardship, moved from Nebraska to Utah to make a living. Mr. Dern also had to discontinue his studies and engage in business to support himself. His first job was as a bookkeeper at the Mercur Gold Mining Company. Because the work was simple, he devoted his spare time to studying metallurgy and engineering. Sixteen years later, the company merged with other gold mines. Seeing Mr. Dern's great potential, the directors promoted him to assistant manager and treasurer. A year later, he was promoted again to general manager, a position he held until the mine closed in 1913. Mr. Dern gained prominence in American politics after being elected as a Senator for Utah. Because of his competence and initiative, he was highly valued by President Roosevelt, who entrusted him with the important responsibility of leading the U.S. Army. His untimely death from heart disease is truly a misfortune for the United States. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

At the Pacific Conference, The Issue of Military Deployments in the Far East Russian and Japanese Representatives Engage in Fierce Debate, Japan Insists on Revising the Nine-Power Treaty, Refuses to Submit to the Hague Court for Interpretation

Yosemite The Pacific Institute continued its roundtable conference today. Heated debate erupted between the Japanese and Russian representatives. The Japanese representative demanded that the Soviet Russian representative explain whether the number of Soviet troops stationed in the Far East exceeded the total number of Japanese troops. The Soviet Russian representative admitted that this claim was not without basis but stated that he did not know the exact figures and would try to find out before reporting to the conference. Both representatives insisted that their respective countries' military strength was purely for defensive purposes. A British representative today proposed that Pacific nations establish a regional security pact with military and economic sanctions, similar to the proposal made yesterday by former French Prime Minister Sarraut. However, other British representatives did not support this proposal. The roundtable conference also determined that the only weapon of the League of Nations for maintaining peace is economic sanctions, which should be implemented swiftly by all countries to be effective. (National Telegram, 27th)

Yosemite The Japanese representative to the Pacific Institute today refused to submit the Nine-Power Treaty to the International Court of Justice at The Hague for interpretation, stating that no country in the world would be willing to submit issues related to its national lifeline to any court for adjudication. He insisted on convening a special conference to revise the treaty, claiming that since the Nine-Power Treaty was established, the only provision that had been implemented was the abolition of foreign post offices in China, which undermined the Chinese postal system. The reduction of the Chinese army had not been implemented, and foreign powers had not yet gradually relinquished their concessions. Since the rise of Soviet Russia, many new problems had arisen in the Pacific region that could not have been foreseen when the Nine-Power Treaty was signed. It is now necessary to convene a special conference to study these issues in detail, he said. (National Telegram, 27th)

New Japanese Ambassador to Russia, Mr. Shigemitsu, Speaks of his Aspirations, Striving to Adjust Relations Between the Two Countries in a Spirit of Non-Aggression and Non-Threat

(Tokyo) Mr. Shigemitsu Aoi, who had been recuperating in the Aharahara area, was officially appointed as the Ambassador to Russia by the government on the 27th. On the morning of the 28th, at 11:00 AM, he returned to Tokyo to meet with Foreign Minister Arita and receive the official credentials of the appointed ambassador. In the afternoon of the 27th, at his villa in Aharahara, Mr. Shigemitsu spoke to reporters about his aspirations, stating that Japan's policy towards Russia was of great importance. Japan's continental policy is based on its policies towards China and Russia. Therefore, Japan-Russia relations are a matter of great concern for the Japanese national life. I have always believed that diplomacy with Russia is an important issue, and I have constantly promoted its importance to various sectors of society. I also believe that the government has a definite policy towards Soviet Russia, which, as Foreign Minister Arita stated in his speech to the Diet, is based on the spirit of non-threat and non-aggression. However, since Soviet Russia has expanded its military deployment in the Far East, Japan has also had to expand its military capabilities to counter it. The opinions of some people in the country are entirely in favor of a non-aggression treaty, but it is doubtful whether the timing is right now. In short, the key to the policy towards Russia lies in how to implement the nationally agreed policy consistently in all aspects. However, the key to opening up Japan-Russia diplomacy is for the Japanese people to pay attention to Soviet affairs and study its various issues, which is most necessary. Deepening the Japanese public's understanding of the Soviet Union will naturally lead to an opportunity to resolve various problems. It is reported that after Ambassador Shigemitsu exchanges opinions with the Foreign Ministry and the Army and Navy authorities, he will travel to Manchuria in late September to investigate the border situation. He is expected to officially take office in November. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 28th)

Border Clashes Occur Frequently, Japan and Russia Exchange Protests, The Potapovka Incident, Russia Announces the Truth

(Moscow) According to reports from Khabarovsk, on the 26th of this month, a team of Soviet border guards in the Potapovka area on the Soviet-Manchurian border was watering their horses by the Ussuri River when they were suddenly fired upon by the "Manchurian" side. The incident occurred at 2:45 PM. Border guards at the Potapovka station were leading their horses to the river to drink when they were bombarded with light machine guns and rifles. The shooting came from a distance of 300 meters, from the direction of Dongning City on the opposite bank. The shooting lasted for 20 minutes, resulting in the death of three horses and the injury of one. Soviet border guards witnessed Japanese and "Manchurian" troops firing together. After the shooting, they fled into Dongning City. Soviet troops did not return fire. (TASS dispatch, 27th)

(Moscow) Regarding the incident on the 26th of this month in which Japanese and "Manchurian" troops opened fire on Soviet border guards near Potapovka, Mr. Kozlovsky of the Soviet Union lodged a protest with the Japanese Chargé d'Affaires in Moscow today. (TASS dispatch, 27th)

(Tokyo) Regarding the illegal border crossing by Soviet cavalry near Dongning, the Ministry of the Army received a detailed telegram from the Kwantung Army on the 28th, clarifying the incident. According to the report, in light of the recent surge in illegal border crossings by the Soviets, the Japanese garrison stationed there dispatched a unit to monitor the border. They discovered 20 Soviet cavalrymen crossing the Ussuri River and intruding into Manchurian territory. A Japanese officer ordered them to stop in Russian and warned that they would be shot if they did not comply. However, the Soviet soldiers ignored the warning and continued to advance across the border. The Japanese commander then ordered his troops to open fire, driving them back across the border. This action was taken to suppress illegal activities. However, the attitude of Soviet soldiers on the border has recently deteriorated significantly. They have repeatedly engaged in illegal shooting at the Japanese garrison. Since June, there have been dozens of incidents with hundreds of bullets fired at the Japanese side, causing the situation to worsen. Although serious protests have been lodged repeatedly, the Soviet side has shown no intention of reflecting on its actions. Foreign Minister Arita has also lodged a serious protest, demanding that the Soviet side reflect on its actions. However, the Russian side has disregarded Japan's protest and shown no intention of reflecting on its actions. If such illegal behavior continues in the future, the situation may inevitably escalate. The responsibility will not lie with Japan. The Japanese side is closely monitoring the situation. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 28th)

The Mystery of Stalin's Speech, Source of London Evening Newspaper's Information

(London) The London Evening Standard reported today that radio listeners here received a broadcast from Moscow at 4:00 AM on Wednesday, in which General Tukhachevsky introduced Army Chief Voroshilov to speak to the Soviet Army. After that, another person spoke. Although his name was not reported, his voice was immediately recognized as Stalin. He said, "We are now on the eve of major events. You can be called upon at any time to sacrifice your lives to defend the birthplace of the proletariat. The enemy is armed and ready, so you must prepare quickly." Although Moscow has denied that Stalin gave a speech to the army, the Daily Mail still carried yesterday's news today. (National Telegram, 28th)

General Secretary of the British Trade Union Congress Speaks on the Current Situation in the Soviet Union, Stalin Seizes Total Power and Eliminates Dissent, Actively Expanding Military Preparations to Defend Against German Invasion

(London) General Secretary Citrine of the British Trades Union Congress recently gave a speech at the Literary Association here, in which he researched the current and future situation of the Soviet Union. He briefly stated that although the implementation of democratic political systems and various principles in the Soviet Union still has a long way to go, it has indeed made much progress in other aspects. "The Soviet Union is dominated by the psychology that other countries may invade it, so its national policy is driven by this. At this moment, the threat of war has come to the Soviet Union. In the country's view, a German invasion is inevitable, so it is expanding its army and also announcing preparations to add airplanes to its air force, striving to match the combined strength of the air forces of other countries. In my view, the German government has repeatedly and clearly refused to conclude an agreement guaranteeing the security of the Soviet Union. The intention is not difficult to imagine. Is the Soviet Union's preparedness without reason?

Citrine went on to mention the recent counter-revolutionary case in Moscow, saying that the trial resulted in the death penalty for all sixteen defendants. He was shocked by this matter. Looking back to the beginning of the October Revolution in 1917, Lenin, Trotsky, Zinoviev, Kamenev, Rykov, Stalin, and Tomsky were all founding fathers. Today, some have died of illness, some have committed suicide, some have been exiled, and some have been executed by their comrades. The only one who remains is Stalin. The significance of this counter-revolutionary case may be to eliminate dissent and use the corpses of the sixteen defendants as a warning to make the people of the country take it as a lesson and dare not hold dissenting opinions again. From now on, Stalin's power will be greater than ever before. In my view, Soviet Russia is currently ruled by a small number of people, and the masses have no participation in politics, which is no different from other dictatorships. My view is fixed and unwavering. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

Germany Extends Military Service Term, Aimed at Russia, Not France, Schacht Explains to French Authorities, Talks Focus on Economic Issues

According to the newspaper's diplomatic correspondent, Schacht's discussions with French authorities in recent days have focused on various economic issues, such as currency stabilization, commercial loans, and raw materials. Political issues, especially Germany's demand for the return of colonies, have also been mentioned. In addition, Schacht explained Germany's Führer Hitler's anti-communism to the French authorities. The Morning Post and L'ECHO DE PARIS also commented on Schacht's visit, but believed that it had no political implications. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

Schacht Concludes Visit to France, Flies Back to Berlin Yesterday

(Paris) Dr. Schacht's visit to meet with French authorities has lasted several days. He is scheduled to take a flight back to Berlin at 2:15 PM today. Before his departure, he went to the Prime Minister's office to bid farewell to Prime Minister Blum. He told our reporter, "I am very pleased to have met with Prime Minister Blum. I am particularly delighted with the satisfactory outcome of this trip." (Havas dispatch, 28th)

France to Ask Russia for Explanation on Lowering Conscription Age

The Soviet government's decision to take this action was made a few days before Germany extended the military service period. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

Russia and Germany Attack Each Other, Russian Newspaper Condemns Germany as "Fascist Bandits"

(Moscow) Izvestia today published an editorial that harshly criticized Germany, even more so than German newspapers criticize Soviet Russia. The article, titled "Fascist Bandits," attacked German Propaganda Minister Goebbels and Chief of the Secret Police Himmler, saying that in recent years German newspapers have systematically fabricated and spread slander about Soviet Russia, with the aim of making the German people accept the bandits' agenda contained in Hitler's book Mein Kampf, which has become the bible of brown assassins, torturers, secret police, and arsonists. Fierce Battles in Northern Spain, Both Armies Reach Stalemate, Rebel Attacks Fail Twice, Government Troops Make Slight Progress

Andaye, Southern France Since the outbreak of fighting in the area around Irun in northern Spain, both sides have engaged in fierce battles for many days, but still remain at a stalemate. At 7:30 AM this morning, several units of the Foreign Legion belonging to the rebel army launched a fierce attack on the Duriarte mountain range, hoping to occupy it. They clashed with government troops. At 10:00 AM, the rebel artillery resumed heavy bombardment of Irun City. Both sides' air forces also launched sorties. Three government aircraft and three rebel aircraft engaged in combat in the sky. At the same time, the rebel warship "España" and the government's Guadalupe fortress exchanged fire, with a hail of bullets. The battle situation was extremely fierce. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

Irun Our correspondent reports exclusively that another fierce battle broke out in the vicinity of this area this afternoon. After government troops repelled the rebels, they launched a counterattack starting at 5:00 PM, advancing several hundred meters. At the same time, the artillery fired on the rebel positions at the foot of Mount Uriat, causing panic in the rebel rear. The situation returned to silence in the evening, but the sound of artillery shells fired by government troops occasionally broke the silence. The rebel actions seemed to be greatly hindered by the government artillery fire. At the same time, several rebel aircraft flew from Burgos City to this area, circling several times, seemingly conducting aerial reconnaissance. The rebel cruiser "España" occasionally opened fire on the Guadalupe fortress. Furthermore, San Sebastian has dispatched a large number of reinforcements who are rushing here to strengthen the defenses. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

Andaye Spanish government troops and rebel troops again engaged in fierce fighting today to seize Irun and San Sebastian. The rebels were again frustrated. After the government artillery began to bombard fiercely, the rebels' two-pronged attacks were repelled, forcing them to abandon their strategy of attacking along the main road from Pamplona to Irun. They later attempted to attack the side slopes of Mount Duriarte but were also frustrated. When reinforcements from the Burgos rebels arrived in the afternoon, the rebels made some progress in the mountains but failed to break through the government's superior position. As evening approached, the rebel artillery fire gradually weakened, and both sides seemed to want to rest briefly, so they withdrew their frontline troops. However, the rebels claimed that the former leader of the military occupied the town of Pantanaravilla near Badasa, and that government aircraft bombed the hospital in Jaca. It is reported that the local garrison commander stated that if government aircraft continued to drop bombs on the hospital, the local authorities intended to execute five government troops imprisoned in the town. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

Rebel Army Occupies Key Terrain in Somo Mountain Area North of Beijing; Surprise Night Attack Overturns Control of Mountain Ridge

A radio station belonging to the rebel army in Burgos broadcast a report yesterday stating that the rebel army had defeated government troops in the Somo Mountain area north of Beijing and immediately occupied the Navacerrada Pass. The area overlooks the Lozoya River valley and is strategically important. This newspaper's special correspondent has learned the details of the battle as follows: Three companies of the rebel army departed from the city of Guadarrama at the northern foot of Somo Mountain on Sunday of this week (the 23rd), intending to seize several strategically important locations to allow the main force to advance directly towards Madrid. After departing, the road was full of steep mountains and difficult terrain. Some mountain peaks were still covered in snow. As night fell, they took advantage of the darkness to sneak along, winding their way for more than seven hours, enduring many hardships before reaching the enemy's position. The position was the Navacerrada Pass, where government troops had set up camp on the mountaintop. The area was surrounded by deep trenches and full of machine guns, resembling a fortress. Under the cover of the dark, the rebel army advanced, reaching within 300 meters of the government troops' position. As dawn approached, they arrived at the front of the government troops' position and immediately charged with bayonets fixed, supported by continuous artillery fire. At the same time, three squadrons of aircraft flew overhead at an altitude of 500 meters, providing support. Each squadron consisted of four three-engine bombers, either opening fire with machine guns or dropping bombs. The government troops were suddenly attacked from above and below, and in a state of panic, quickly collapsed and fled, abandoning the mountaintop. More than sixty corpses were left behind. The retreating troops fired several volleys of shots as cover. The rebel army immediately raised the red and yellow flag (the national flag stipulated by the rebel army) on a tall tree on the mountaintop and sang patriotic songs to celebrate their victory. (Havas News Agency, 27th)

Various Frontlines: Both Sides Claim Victory; Oviedo Surrounded by Government Troops

Lisbon: The Spanish Civil War continues intensely today. Radio stations on both sides are claiming victory. The rebel radio station in Cordoba claimed that after a major battle, the rebel army had defeated the attacking government forces and captured countless spoils of war. The Madrid government radio station claimed that the artillery had destroyed the rebel radio station in Oviedo. Government troops in the Malaga area are advancing steadily. The navy is bombarding Palma. The rebels besieged in Palma sent a telegram to General Franco, commander of the southern front, informing him that the situation was critical, morale was low, and they would surrender if reinforcements did not arrive. The rebel radio station in Cadiz claimed that rebel aircraft had dropped multiple 100-pound bombs on the bullring in Madrid on Tuesday, destroying many vehicles gathered there. It also claimed that 150 aristocratic women and 300 officers and soldiers sympathetic to the rebels in Madrid had been massacred. However, General Queipo de Llano also announced on the rebel radio station in Seville that he had ordered that for every rebel executed, five Marxist families would be killed in retaliation. "The word 'mercy' is no longer in my dictionary," he said. (Guomin News Agency, 27th)

Burgos: This newspaper's special correspondent has learned the following about the war situation on various fronts: (1) The city of Oviedo in the northwest is surrounded by government troops. Three columns of rebel troops have been dispatched to provide assistance and lift the siege. (2) The government troops' positions in the province of Guipúzcoa in the north are gradually being surrounded by rebel troops. At the same time, the cruiser "Admiral Cervera" is bombarding the fortresses of San Sebastián. (3) On the eastern front in the province of Aragon, government troops attempted to besiege the city of Daroca, but were repelled by rebel troops. (4) In the Guadarrama Mountains north of Beijing, three government aircraft were shot down by rebel troops. Three other aircraft flew from Madrid and surrendered to the rebel troops. There is no other news. (5) The air force belonging to the rebel army flew to the city of Toledo south of Beijing and bombed and destroyed a munitions factory there. Of all the national munitions factories, this is the only one still in the hands of government troops. (6) On the southern front in the province of Cordoba, a unit of rebel troops engaged government troops in the city of Palma del Río. The government troops resisted fiercely, but eventually collapsed, abandoning many corpses and retreating. The rebel troops then occupied the city. (Havas News Agency, 27th)

(Paris) The civil war in Spain has resolved the longstanding diplomatic animosity between Spain and Soviet Russia. Mr. Rosenberg, the former Soviet Deputy Representative to the League of Nations in Geneva, arrived in Madrid today to take up his post as Soviet Ambassador. (Reuters, 28th)

(Geneva) League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol issued a statement stating that Mr. Rosenberg, a Russian national and Assistant Secretary of the Secretariat (former Chargé d'Affaires in France), has been appointed by the Soviet government as Ambassador to Spain and has resigned from his current position. It is noted that diplomatic relations between Spain and the Soviet Union were severed after the European War and were only restored on July 27, 1933. However, to date, the two sides have not exchanged ambassadors. (Havas News Agency, 27th)

(London) The British Ambassador to Spain recently suggested that all countries jointly appeal to both sides of the Spanish Civil War to do their utmost to reduce slaughter for the sake of humanity. (London) The Italian government today announced that it has authorized the Finance Minister to issue foreign currency treasury bonds in foreign markets. Italy should find a way to solve this difficulty. Generally speaking, outstanding debts owed by American businesses to Italy should be repaid by Italy as a condition of exchange. Hurricane Hits Southern Korea, Causing Disaster; Material Damage Exceeds 20 Million Yen; Fierce Wind Rare in Recent Years

Busan: The typhoon that struck the southern Korean peninsula on the morning of the 27th affected the areas of North Jeolla Province, North and South Gyeongsang Province, and Gangwon Province. It moved towards the Sea of Japan around dawn on the 28th. Around 2:00 AM on the 28th, Busan experienced a hurricane with a wind speed of 31.4 meters per second, causing railway disruptions, human and livestock casualties, house collapses and flooding, power outages, and disruptions to telegraph and telephone services. Reports of shipwrecks continue to emerge, and the damage appears to be severe. Detailed information is currently unavailable due to communication disruptions. This hurricane is the most severe since the Meiji 37th year, so the amount of damage in southern Korea is feared to exceed 20 million yen. According to a survey by the Gyeongsangnam-do Police Department, the typhoon damage situation within the province is as follows:

One death, 60 injuries, 250 houses collapsed, 500 houses flooded inside, 1,000 houses flooded underneath, 70 ships sunk or damaged. (Allied News Agency, 27th)
