All Customs Child Servants Plead Not to Be Dismissed: Six Have Been Replaced by New Servants: The Entire Group is Panicked and Appeals to the Customs

Datong News: Regarding the rumors circulating outside about the dismissal of the Jianghai Customs child servants, a reporter from Datong News learned yesterday morning that the matter is still under discussion and may be resolved. The situation is recorded as follows:

Brief History of Child Servants: There are currently a total of thirty-three child servants in the Jianghai Customs. They were all hired after passing the shipowner's office examination. It is said that when they were hired, there was a fixed employment period of three years, but it was also said that if their service performance was good, they could be continuously employed. The salary of these child servants is uniformly 16 yuan per month. Among the thirty-three who passed the exam at that time, about ten have been dismissed by the Customs in the past three years, and new child servants have been recruited to supplement them.

Cause of Fermentation: The cause of this turmoil was due to the Customs' past decision to dismiss child servants. Before the official announcement, new child servants must be assigned to replace the duties of the old child servants. Recently, the six child servants of (1) the dispatch room, (2) the customs warehouse, (3) the third section, (4) the fourth section, (5) the visa station, and (6) the signing station have been replaced by new child servants assigned by the customs.

Please Do Not Dismiss: The other child servants, considering that the three-year service period of the majority has expired, and feeling sympathetic, jointly elected representatives to request the customs authorities to exempt them from dismissal. However, the authorities have not expressed any opinion. According to the child servants, their duties are only to sweep, run errands, and deliver documents. As for the reports, they are locked into the safe by the customs officers before being handed over to the child servants for delivery to various departments. Therefore, even if they serve in the customs for life, it is absolutely impossible for them to cheat. Some say that child servants who have served for too long are prone to corruption, but they do not understand the situation.

Special Edition on Sichuan Opera: Accused of Defamation

Shi Chunxuan, a native of Shanghai, age 36, a comedian and standing committee member of the Shanghai Opera Research Association, residing at No. 1, Shen Yu Lane, Huacheng Road, French Concession, through lawyer Jin Yan, filed a suit with the Criminal Division of the Second Special Court, accusing Lu Hancheng, a Sichuanese and manager of the Sichuan Grand Stage at the Xinguang Grand Theater on Ningbo Road, Public Concession, and publisher of the Sichuan Opera Special, along with Sun Jiayu (age 23, from Chengdu, residing at the Sichuan Opera Special office, No. 66, Songshan Road, French Concession) and Liu Zuoxiang (age 32, Sichuanese, residing with Sun Jiayu), of defamation. The indictment states that on August 5, the first day of publication of the Sichuan Opera Special, it contained statements such as "Sichuan opera does not involve absurdity or obscenity, and will definitely not cater to the general social psychology like the current Shanghai opera and other local operas, forgetting the mission of dramatic education." Members of the Shanghai Opera Research Association believe that the Sichuan Opera Special intentionally slandered and defamed the reputation of the entire Shanghai opera community. After deliberation, the association decided to appoint Shi Chunxuan to file the lawsuit, requesting the court to investigate according to law. Upon receiving the indictment, the court, yesterday afternoon, dispatched Judge Sun Peng to the Second Criminal Court to summon the defendants. The plaintiff, Shi Chunxuan, arrived with his lawyer and presented his case. The first defendant, Lu Hancheng, was absent due to illness. The second and third defendants, Sun Jiayu and Liu Zuoxiang, arrived with their defense lawyer. According to Sun and Liu, Sichuan opera has not been in Shanghai for long. Due to language barriers, this special edition was published to facilitate research for fellow villagers and spectators and to improve the quality of performances. It is no different from a prospectus. The Shanghai opera and other local operas mentioned in the special edition are abstract terms and do not specifically refer to the Shanghai Opera Research Association or Shi personally. There is no defamation. We hope to improve drama to fulfill its educational mission. We are new to Shanghai, have no animosity towards the Shi family, and have no grievances with the Shanghai Opera Research Association. How could we harm their reputation? Judge Sun, after reviewing the testimonies, believed that the case was clear. After arguments, he declared the hearing closed and scheduled the verdict for September 2.

Another Lawsuit Against Tongyi Trust Company: Lu Tangcha and Others Representing Over 300 Households, Court Hearing Adjourned

Since the Tongyi Trust Company suddenly collapsed and declared bankruptcy on June 16 of this year, depositors and those who entrusted the company with the safekeeping of government bonds have accused the company of illegal activities. They have filed lawsuits with the First Special Court against the directors and supervisors of Tongyi Company, and sentences have been handed down. These matters have been reported in this newspaper. Recently, Lu Tangcha, Ying Shugui, Wang Meiqing, and others, representing over 300 depositors, have separately hired lawyers Zhang Yifan and Chen Changsheng, as well as accountant Ma Qichang, to file a lawsuit against

Huang Suchu, director and general manager of Tongyi Company, and directors Liu Fangyuan, Xu Jiyi, Zhou Shouliang, Guo Yushang, Liu Rensan, Xiong Muqu, and supervisors Jiang Yizhi, Chuan Zhu Yin, and Wu Jingwen, for violating Articles 231, 232, and 233 of the Company Law, and Article 16, Paragraph 2 of the Savings Bank Law. In addition to requesting legal punishment, they also attached a civil suit, requesting that the defendants and Tongyi Company be jointly responsible for repaying 176,004.67 yuan in national currency. The case has been heard once, but due to the absence of the defendants, it was ordered to be rescheduled. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ye Shengchao

presided over the Fifth Criminal Court for a continued hearing. Only Xu Jiyi, Guo Yushang, Zhou Shouliang, and Fu Zhu Yin among the defendants appeared in court with defense lawyers Xu Shihao and Zuo De. The others were absent. According to the testimony of the four defendants present, they generally did not deny their positions as directors and supervisors, but claimed that they were not very familiar with the company's internal affairs. The company did not provide detailed reports during board meetings, so the truth of the plaintiffs' claims was unclear. Judge Ye then commenced the arguments. The plaintiff's lawyer then detailed the defendants' violations

of the Company Law, stating that the credit and mortgage loans in the asset section of the 1932-34 balance sheets included 978,000 yuan loaned to the Changzhou Tongcheng Yarn Factory and 300,000 yuan loaned to the former Beijing government's Ministry of Finance, all of which were long-term bad debts with no hope of recovery. These were listed as assets to deceive depositors, which constitutes a violation of Article 231, Paragraph 6 of the Company Law. Furthermore, the company's paid-up capital was 1.36 million yuan, and the aforementioned bad debts alone amounted to over one million yuan. This means that before this year,

the remaining capital was only 82,000 yuan. According to the Company Law, if a company's losses reach one-third of its total capital, the directors should immediately convene a shareholders' meeting to report the situation. Although the defendants convened a shareholders' meeting and distributed dividends, they continued to obscure the company's losses, which constitutes a violation of Article 232, Paragraph 1 of the Company Law. Furthermore, if the company's assets are clearly insufficient to cover its debts, the directors should immediately apply for bankruptcy. Since the Changzhou Tongcheng Company's bankruptcy in 1933 resulted in a loss of 978,000 yuan in loans, the company's assets had been depleted three years ago and were insufficient

to cover its debts. This fact was obvious, but the defendants did not apply for bankruptcy according to law, which constitutes a violation of Article 232, Paragraph 7 of the Company Law. Moreover, the savings deposit regulations published by the company in January 1927 stated that the total paid-up capital was 1.7 million yuan, while the asset-liability statement for the 1935 financial year showed a change to 1.36 million yuan, a difference of 340,000 yuan. This indicates that the total amount of paid-up capital was falsely stated when applying for registration, which constitutes a violation of Article 233, Paragraph 1 of the Company Law. Furthermore, according to

Article 8 of the Savings Bank Law, the amount of deposits a savings bank places in other banks shall not exceed one-fifteenth of its total deposits. A review of the defendants' 1935 asset-liability statement shows that the savings department's income was 2,269,942.52 yuan, while the total amount deposited in other banks reached 183,440.41 yuan, exceeding one-fifteenth of the total. Therefore, we request that they be punished according to law and that the civil suit for 176,004.67 yuan be attached. The defendants' defense lawyers then rose to reply, stating that although the defendants present were

nominally directors or supervisors, they were not actually familiar with the company's internal details or the detailed accounts, nor were they executive directors in charge of operations. Therefore, in addition to pleading not guilty, they questioned whether the plaintiff's representatives present were authorized by the claimed 300-plus people, and whether there were authorization letters and supporting documents, which the defendants were not aware of. This point is procedurally flawed. Judge Ye, noting that the issue of the plaintiff's representatives' qualifications required the plaintiff's lawyer to provide supporting documents, adjourned the case to September 3 for a continued hearing in the afternoon.

Public Bus Causes Accident: One Woman Killed, Two Rickshaw Pullers Detained, Bus Driver Also Responsible

At 11:50 PM the night before, a public bus collided with two rickshaws at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Chengdu Road, resulting in the death of a female passenger, Wang Aifen (age 22, from Suzhou, residing at No. 3, Rongkang Lane, Muer Ming Road). According to the police investigation, three rickshaws were traveling side by side from east to west when the accident occurred. The rickshaw occupied by the deceased was pulled by Wu Yuru from Jiangbei, positioned on the outermost side. As they passed the intersection, Li Baofu, also from Jiangbei, attempted to overtake the three vehicles, and a British-owned double-decker bus, No. 15092, driven by Yu Rixian, was speeding towards them. Unable to avoid the collision, the bus struck Li's rickshaw, flipping it over. The driver then turned the bus outwards, but the front of the bus struck the rickshaw pulled by Wu Yuru, flipping it over and injuring Wang. Two Westerners driving by in a car immediately sent Wang to Guangci Hospital, but she died from her injuries at 3:00 AM the next morning. The police, believing that Wu Yuru and Li Baofu were negligent, detained them. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, explained the case and requested that Wu and Li be temporarily detained. Li Baofu testified that there were no three rickshaws traveling side by side. Judge Huang Yuesheng, after reviewing the testimonies, ordered that Wu and Li be detained until next Thursday. Prosecutor Tang from the First Special Court arrived at the center and examined the body. According to the police report, the deceased had been out with her boyfriend, Liang Hebing, from the International Hotel. Liang has now gone to Hong Kong. The deceased's brother, Wang Boying, a secretary in the Shanghai Municipal Government, strongly criticized the public bus driver, Yu Rixian, stating that Yu had conjunctivitis, his eyes were red and swollen, and he did not use the horn. He requested an investigation. Yu Rixian also admitted that he did not use the horn at the time. The police stated that they would conduct a thorough investigation of the case. Prosecutor Tang ruled that the deceased, Wang Aifen, died from injuries sustained in the bus collision. The body was released to her brother, Wang Boying, for burial. The case should be further investigated in detail by the responsible police station.

Gambling Leads to Homicide: Suspect Awaits Sentencing

Weng Zhi, a Chaozhou native residing at No. 10, Yuanfang Lane, Yuanfang Road, worked as a porter at the Jardine Matheson Wharf. On the afternoon of the 13th of this month, around 8:00 PM, he was gambling with Wang Along (a peddler from Ningbo) as a pastime. Wang lost, and after settling accounts with a local beggar, he owed Weng 7 dimes. He paid 8 dimes, but Weng demanded 10 more copper coins, leading to an argument. Weng angrily slapped Wang once on the ear and left. Wang was very unhappy and waited for Weng on Yuanfang Road, McTaggart Road. When Weng arrived, Wang dragged him and punched and kicked him in the chest and abdomen. Weng fell to the ground, and Wang took the opportunity to escape. Weng Zhi was sent to the Jardine Matheson Workshop at No. 351 Broadway Road by fellow villagers Huang Jiaxu and Lin Rizhong. He died at 7:00 AM on the 15th. The Hongkou police station was notified and sent detective Zhao Ziqian to investigate. The body was taken to the forensic examination center on Feilun Road. A prosecutor from the First Special District Court arrived and ordered a forensic examination. The body was released to his wife, Yang, for burial. The suspect, Wang Along, was apprehended by detective Zhao on Minguo Road in the French Concession at 5:45 PM on the 17th and sent to the court for detention. Yesterday, Judge Xiao Xiefei opened the Third Criminal Court for trial. The official stated that the forensic examination revealed that Weng Zhi died from a ruptured intestine in the abdomen. According to the statement from Weng's wife, Yang, her husband told her before his death that he was beaten by Wang Along. Witnesses Huang Jiaxu and Lin Rizhong testified that they witnessed Wang Along beating Weng Zhi. They did not see Weng slap Wang during the gambling. The two beggars testified that Wang Along lost 4 dimes to Weng and 3 dimes to them. There was a settlement of accounts, but they did not know about the fight. Wang Along insisted that Weng should not have slapped him and said disrespectful things. Therefore, he became angry and caused the tragedy. It was not intentional and he asked for leniency. After Judge Xiao appointed a lawyer to defend the defendant and the Shanghai Municipal Council lawyer, Zhang Shizhu, to argue, the judge ordered that he be remanded in custody to await sentencing.

Statistics on New Subsidiary Coins from the Mint

According to the Shenshi News Agency, after the Ministry of Finance implemented the legal tender policy and issued a notice to exchange legal tender within a specified period on November 4 of last year, the Ministry ordered the Central Mint to mint hard subsidiary coins for circulation in the market to support the implementation of legal tender. Starting from February 10 of this year, these decimal new subsidiary coins were first used in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. As of now, with the exception of Guizhou Province, where the new subsidiary coins have not yet been used, and remote rural areas, the larger cities and towns in other provinces have already circulated them. By the end of July, the Central Mint had minted the following quantities of nickel and copper new subsidiary coins: 17.78 million 20-cent coins, 30.02 million 10-cent coins, 57.4 million 5-cent coins, 143.02 million 1-cent coins, and 41.68 million 1/2-cent coins. The statistics of monthly output since February are as follows: (February) 890,000 20-cent nickel coins, 2.7 million 10-cent nickel coins, 4.68 million 5-cent nickel coins, 25.5 million 1-cent copper coins, 8.52 million 1/2-cent copper coins; (March) 4.09 million 20-cent nickel coins, 2.28 million 10-cent nickel coins, 280,000 5-cent nickel coins, 18 million 1-cent copper coins, 16.81 million 1/2-cent copper coins; (April) 860,000 20-cent nickel coins, 1.9 million 10-cent nickel coins, 6.8 million 5-cent nickel coins, 27.34 million 1-cent copper coins, 11.16 million 1/2-cent copper coins; (May) 2.92 million 20-cent nickel coins, 6.26 million 10-cent nickel coins, 19.8 million 5-cent nickel coins, 24.26 million 1-cent copper coins, 1.56 million 1/2-cent copper coins; (June) 2.74 million 20-cent nickel coins, 4.72 million 10-cent nickel coins, 18.44 million 5-cent nickel coins, 23.38 million 1-cent copper coins, 2.12 million 1/2-cent copper coins; (July) 5.68 million 20-cent nickel coins, 12.16 million 10-cent nickel coins, 7.4 million 5-cent nickel coins, 34.54 million 1-cent copper coins, 520,000 1/2-cent copper coins.

Record of Our National Athletes' Participation (Letter 10) Special Correspondent Feng Youzhen

100-Meter Final

The 100-meter final turned into a white-hot bloody battle. It was truly a magnificent spectacle. The two black sprinters fought to the death, thrilling the more than 100,000 spectators in the audience, who were beside themselves with excitement. The six generals who qualified for the final rested for an hour after the semi-finals and took to the field again at 5:00 PM. The audience cheered and applauded thunderously. The six were lined up, with Owens in the first lane, Strömberg in the second, Borchmeyer in the third, Osendarp in the fourth, Wykoff in the fifth, and Metcalfe in the sixth. As they took their positions and prepared to start, the entire audience held their breath and was silent. At the sound of the gun, Owens, Wykoff, and Osendarp moved forward in a line. Metcalfe started more slowly, falling behind by one step. Owens quickened his light pace, sprinting like a fly. At 60 meters, he was one meter ahead of the others.

Metcalfe, who was in fourth place at the time, also quickened his pace, fighting bravely. The competition was fierce. At the finish line, he was only a shoulder behind Owens. Osendarp was half a step behind. Veteran Wykoff's golden age had passed, and he only beat Borchmeyer by a chest to take fourth place. Owens' time was 10.3 seconds, equaling the world record jointly held by Canadian Williams and American Tolan. However, it was still not as fast as his own time of 10.2 seconds in the previous race. This 100-meter race included 12 preliminary races, 4 quarter-final races, 2 semi-final races, and 1 final race. Not a single participant jumped the gun, demonstrating that the world's athletes are extraordinary. The final results are as follows:

(1) Owens (USA) 10.3 seconds

(2) Metcalfe (USA) 10.4 seconds

(3) Osendarp (Netherlands) 10.5 seconds

(4) Wykoff (USA)

(5) Borchmeyer (France)

Subsequently, the situation gradually eased, the two armies in Guangdong and Guangxi were demobilized, and the market price soared, reaching a new high on July 24th. After that, the situation became unpredictable again, followed by the serious situation of the Sui East issue, and income tax was also applied to the interest on public prices. According to the August course, the highest and lowest prices differed by 7 yuan to 9 yuan. The fluctuations will continue to rise and fall within this range. On Cultural Aggression, Talking from Shanghai Local Supplements, by Meng Ruo

The "friendly nation's" aggression against our country is multifaceted. Politics, military affairs, economy, and culture are all actively pursued when the opportunity arises. Political and military policies have already achieved considerable results, while the economy is being "promoted." As for culture, there has also been considerable attention paid to it recently. They plan to establish a library in Shanghai one moment, and propose to establish a testing ground in Beiping the next. In short, they try to get their hands on any place that can "promote" culture.

Recently, there has been a rumor that the "friendly nation" is opening schools in various parts of our country. The Southern Taiwan Governor's Office has decided to establish a five-year Class A commercial school in Xiamen, enrolling Japanese and Taiwanese youth who aspire to be active in South China and Southeast Asia, teaching them Chinese, and also enrolling Chinese students. In the north, a certain Taiwanese resident in Beiping has contacted a certain cultural organization and some people in Chinese academic circles, planning to set up a Sino-Japanese university there. The establishment funds and foundation will be allocated from the "friendly nation's" unreturned Boxer Indemnity funds.

This is clearly a form of cultural aggression. Recently, the "friendly nation" has been shouting about "Northern Ningbo and Southern Advancement." Opening a commercial school in Xiamen is a preparation for "Southern Advancement." In order to implement the Southern Advancement policy, they are vigorously encouraging Taiwanese to immigrate to South China. Now, by training a group of "vanguards" who aspire to be active in South China and Southeast Asia, the force of aggression will be even greater. The "friendly nation" has established a commercial school in Shanghai, and many graduates have been sent to inland China to conduct on-the-ground investigations of social and economic conditions. The commercial school in Xiamen undoubtedly has the same mission.

The Sino-Japanese University in Beiping, emerging at this time, is even more noteworthy. In recent years, the number of Chinese students going to the "friendly nation" to study has increased day by day. Among these many students, there must be many who are truly seeking knowledge. However, it cannot be said that there are none with ulterior motives. They have seen through this point and simply established a university in China, partly to "promote" culture and partly to "manufacture" some "Japan experts" to serve them. Achieving two goals with one action, why not do it?

There is even "better" news: the "friendly nation's" cultural work is not only focused on intellectuals, but will also benefit the common people. The other day, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs held a meeting to discuss cultural undertakings towards China, because in the past, they had focused too much on academics and had little contact with the Chinese people, and therefore had not achieved full results. Therefore, it was decided to establish industrial research institutes in Jinan and Tianjin. This is complementary to economic policy. Recently, they have been focusing on economic development in northern China. The establishment of industrial research institutes is to guide farmers and improve industries. This effort is much more beneficial than academics. No wonder a group of "friendly nation" dignitaries often issue high-sounding theories about stabilizing the lives of North China's farmers.

Cultural aggression is so fierce. What methods should we use to resist it?

The Story of an Old Woman, by Xiu Yang

After dinner, this square is a good place for the public to cool off and chat.

In the countryside, dinner is not eaten after sunset. The evening glow hangs in the sky like festive lanterns, and the evening breeze blowing from the top of the old elm tree awakens people from the fatigue of the day's work. Several farmers who like to have a drink temporarily gather some leftover dishes and sit freely in a corner of the square. The scent of rice fields is carried by the evening breeze, and they are already looking forward to this year's harvest.

Some news heard from teahouses in the city is good material for long cool nights. A simple story, a legend from the newspaper ten or fifteen days ago, they talk about it with great interest. Day after day, it gradually transforms into a strange story, and even the person who started telling the story can no longer figure out its origin and end. The years of the villagers are filled with joy before the autumn harvest.

This year, there is an old woman who is good at telling stories in this square. According to her, her hometown is in a province hundreds of miles away, and she has wandered to this town to visit her son. When a person with a foreign accent appears in this town, there is always an inexplicable rumor. When the old woman settled down, someone spread the rumor that a certain party had come to spy, and that she was investigating the town's strengths and weaknesses, and that a certain party would soon come to rob the town. This rumor did make the people in the town very panic. They are not afraid of being robbed, they are all poor, but everyone has a hope pinned on the fields they are working hard to cultivate. Before the harvest, they are unwilling to give up and flee for their lives. If it is just the time to thresh wheat, how can they escape with these hard-earned properties? So, some courageous women made friends with the old woman. The old woman spins yarn at home every day. She is very kind. She is an old woman who has experienced the world, and she often helps young people solve many difficult things. Her ability to tell stories makes the people in the whole town get closer. When the old woman realized that her arrival in the town was being seen as a secret, she began to tell her own story.

——Her hometown is north of the Yangtze River. She married her husband at the age of fifteen, because poor families are unwilling to keep their daughters for long to share the profits. Her husband sells various medicinal materials in the five northern provinces, and it is rare for him to stay at home for a month a year, but their relationship is very good. She gave birth to a son when she was twenty years old. Giving birth to a son in the first pregnancy is a great joy. Her husband did not go out to do business for more than half a year that year because of the birth of his son. At that time, people often came to her house to make trouble with her husband. Those people were her husband's companions.

One day, when the sky was just beginning to dawn, they came and took her husband away. At the time of the Ya Pai, someone came to tell her that her husband had been hacked to death by the pond three miles away. This was a bolt from the blue. She ran over there crying with her child who was a few months old. She also ran to the local official to demand that the murderer be apprehended. This murder case was solved three years later. It turned out that her husband and that group of people were doing a secret business in the five northern provinces. She gave birth to a son and stayed at home for half a year, and his companions thought that he wanted to quit, which was detrimental to them, so they wanted to kill him.

After her husband died, the old woman took her three-year-old child and wandered around. She worked as a beggar, a servant, and a female worker. She did all kinds of lowly work for women, and she raised her son to adulthood.

But when a civil war began, she was working as a sock weaver within the firing line, and her son was arrested. When the war ended, her son did not return. She spent more than ten years searching for his whereabouts in every province and every county in the north, even if she could see her son's bones. During that period, she endured a harder life and all kinds of humiliation.

Now the north is like another world. After suffering for more than fifty years, she is unwilling to see that kind of cruel massacre again, so she came south to this town.

This story aroused the sympathy of the people in the town. They had all grown up in hard times, and they had also suffered the same fate as the old woman. They vaguely felt that their hopes had been dashed, and farming was no longer their lifelong profession... The old woman's story gradually alienated their will.

Page 20

Words by the Lakeside, by Lü Gang

Recently, I have often liked to take a nap, perhaps because life makes me feel too tired? Every day I run back from a long way, and that's how I waste an afternoon. You say, "Work hard! Laziness deserves a beating." But no matter how I resolve to "work hard," the result is still the same. Sometimes I scold myself very harshly, but sometimes when I think about it calmly, I feel that the surrounding environment really makes it impossible for me to be quiet...

I really want to escape this atmosphere, but in fact there is no way for me to do so. So sometimes I have a leisurely mood and look at the sunset glow in front of the window. These few days, the sky at dusk has been very beautiful, and I occasionally think of the distant view of that dusk I saw in the carriage... This kind of mood may be abnormal, but I feel a bit of a "stealing leisure from busy" sensation... I fight with a contradictory psychology all day long. Therefore, I often think of the "dual personality" you mentioned: "One side is innocent, lively, enthusiastic, happy, gentle... but the other side is absolutely different: melancholy, sentimental, quiet, cold, stubborn..." I feel that a person's life is just a constant struggle between these contradictions. Therefore, no wonder some people attribute a person's innate personality to the environment.

The living environment has been a bit dim lately, and the more we feel distressed, the more the environment feels "unclear." Sometimes I also have a quirk like you, liking to sit alone quietly and remain silent. So you said this in a letter when you were sick: "...I always like to stay alone in the quiet, dim garden, without moving or making a sound. I often want to run to the mountains or the seaside to cry to my heart's content, or just bury myself in the magnificent sea, or break myself to pieces in the abyss..." These words moved me very much and aroused my sympathy. We said that after a certain period we would go to the beach to see the vast sea, but we have not yet finished this matter. We are dragging on day by day in a gloomy environment and in a busy life. ——How can a young person survive in this "prematurely aged" atmosphere?

A person is sometimes very contradictory. A year ago, I lived quietly in a bustling city, and I felt extremely empty. I had no way to pass the long days, and I read an extremely precious book from beginning to end seven or eight times. Now, I am so busy all day long that I don't even have the opportunity to read, and I still feel extremely empty.

Someone talked about Tolstoy's extraordinary temperament and enthusiasm, and I didn't quite agree with this person's words. I remained silent. I thought of the passage of Tolstoy that we had debated repeatedly; I now have a new interpretation, that is a most noble feeling for people... Perhaps you will no longer stubbornly argue with me about this. Of course, this debate is not without meaning. I am often afraid that enthusiasm will damage reason. So I still agree with the opinion you said: emotions should not be released casually, but should be restrained.

The impulse of enthusiasm often kills a useful person. It is a pot of fire, and it will cause disaster when it cannot be contained.

Often, enthusiasm is a great driving force for promoting work, but it is only possible when holding a pure sense of career. However, now, although we have not lost enthusiasm for the cause we are loyal to, and we still have youthful energy and confidence, I feel a bit of unbearable fatigue under this gloomy situation.

I believe you will suspect that I am sick. If it is really a disease, it doesn't matter, because I often forget my body. Just as I forget my individuality in a crowd. But in fact, from my physique, there is no way that there would be no signs of disease. I feel that as long as this tired mood can take a breath in the bright sky, it will be enough.

I looked at the sky, the sun had already set, but the beautiful sunset glow had not yet appeared.

Movie and Drama News

"China Travel" Will Perform for the Second Time

Recently rehearsing, producing scenery, busy state of busyness. From September 3rd, the "China Traveling Troupe" led by Mr. Tang Huaiqiu will continue to perform at the Carlton. After performing at the Carlton, they went to Beijing to perform at the "World" and "Capital" theaters, and returned to Shanghai with praise last month. After a short rest, they immediately began rehearsing. Mr. Tang also telegraphed Dr. Chen Mian, the director of the troupe in Beiping, to come to Shanghai. Mr. Chen specially wrote a new play "Motherland" for the troupe, which tells the tragic history of the demise of the European "Flanders" country in the fifteenth and sixteenth centuries. Mr. Chen will personally direct it, and more than 30 actors will participate, including the troupe's new members Tian Zizhao, Pan Bingxin, Du Guang, Jin Qian, Zheng Ling, Bai Dun, female members Lingzi, Meng Fen, Yan Ke, Bai Yan, etc., as well as the original members who stayed with the troupe. Rehearsals have now been completed. Set designer Wu Jingping and others have created sets in the medieval style, including several scenes such as castles and streets, all of which are rare and great sets on the stage. The sonorous lines and gorgeous costumes are even more impressive. In addition, Mr. Yang Hansheng, a playwright of the "China Stage Association," wrote the play "The Eve" based on the recent situation in North China. The structure is exceptionally wonderful. Mr. Tang Huaiqiu went to Beijing to obtain the performance rights of the play, and is now rehearsing day and night. Because of the realistic plot of the play, it will surely move people's emotions when the time comes.

As for the play "Thunderstorm," it has long had a large number of continuations in literature. The audience praised the last performance, and it was still full until the last show. After the performance was stopped, the audience sent letters and telegrams requesting a continuation of the performance, but it was not possible because the theater was rented to Westerners to show British films. Therefore, it was decided to perform it again at the Carlton to live up to the audience's support.

Maochang Optical Company has always been regarded as a pioneering optical store. Liyuan Farm Milk Sales are Booming: The milk produced by Liyuan Farm at 2746 Zhongshan Road, West Shanghai, has always been known for its purity and rich nutrition. Recently, the Shanghai Municipal Council's Health Department, in accordance with new regulations, has re-issued the farm with a Grade A TT milk license, that is, Grade A sterilized milk. Furthermore, the cattle have been tested for tuberculosis and showed no reaction. This milk is produced from cattle free of tuberculosis and has undergone sterilization procedures, ensuring double hygiene protection. As a result, the demand for milk from this farm is very enthusiastic.

Education News

President Wang Discusses the Significance of Establishing the Jiangxi Zhongzheng Medical College: National Shortage of Medical Talents, Especially Easy to Establish a College in Jiangxi Province

(Nanjing, 18th) President Wang told a reporter from the Central News Agency on the morning of the 28th, about the significance of preparing to establish the National Zhongzheng Medical College in Nanchang. There are three points: (1) The Ministry of Education recognizes that there is a shortage of medical talents in China, and there are still few medical schools and colleges in the country, and the talents cultivated are limited, which is far from meeting the current needs. Therefore, in recent years, the Ministry of Education has been striving to improve the quality and quantity of medical education. In addition to sending personnel to inspect the original colleges and ordering them to improve, the establishment of dental colleges and the preparation for the establishment of pharmaceutical colleges are all determined according to actual needs. The intention of establishing this college is also based on this. (2) The establishment of a medical college must have sufficient equipment and a complete hospital for students to practice. Now the new hospital built by the National Economic Council in Nanchang has been completed, so the preparation of this college is easier. (3) Jiangxi Province has been making rapid progress in local construction in recent years, and there is an urgent need for public health administrators. The Jiangxi Provincial Government can also raise funds to assist in the preparation of the college, so the college council has made this decision. As for the Ministry of Education sending personnel to Jiangxi to prepare a department, the Ministry of Education is considering candidates.

Another telegram said that President Wang went to the Ministry on the morning of the 28th to deal with Ministry affairs. Lei Zhen and Huang Longxian, secretary of the Ministry of Education, arrived in Beijing by boat from Xun on the afternoon of the 28th.

Overview of Compulsory Education in Guangdong Province: More Than 600,000 Yuan Raised This Year

Guangdong Province has been able to pay attention to compulsory education. Therefore, in 1928, the Provincial Compulsory Education Committee was established to assist in the implementation of compulsory education. The number of schools and students has increased year by year. In 1931, there were 18,969 elementary schools in the province with 1,098,965 students. After the promulgation of the first three-year education administration plan, it progressed even more rapidly. By 1934, there were a total of 12,754 elementary schools with 1,469,406 students. Compared with 1931, the number of schools increased by 3,785 and the number of students increased by 370,441. In 1935, the overall situation was planned, and measures were formulated. Impoverished counties were given subsidies, while wealthy counties were required to manage themselves. A total of 70 counties in the province received subsidies: 20 counties received subsidies to open two ordinary elementary schools and four short-term elementary schools, 20 counties received subsidies to open nine short-term elementary schools, and 30 counties received subsidies to open five short-term elementary schools. The 20 relatively wealthy counties did not need subsidies and were ordered to raise funds on their own. The three newly established counties in Qiongdong and the jurisdiction of the Nanshan Administration also received special subsidies. The source of the subsidies was partly from the provincial treasury and partly from central government subsidies. The province subsidized the opening of 40 ordinary elementary schools and 160 short-term elementary schools, while the central government subsidized the opening of 250 short-term elementary schools. The Provincial Compulsory Education Committee has repeatedly decided on the implementation of compulsory education in the province in 1936, and the original subsidy measures will be maintained and improved. This year, the central government has ordered a subsidy of 220,000 yuan for the province's compulsory education, and the province has raised funds for compulsory education itself, following the central government's regulations, and has raised more than 100,000 yuan. Therefore, it is not difficult to achieve the original plan for the promotion of compulsory education in the province this year.

Aquatic Institutions Telegraphically Request to Maintain the Tianjin Aquatic School

(Central News Agency) The Tianjin Aquatic School has achieved remarkable results since its establishment and has a long history. Now the Hebei Provincial Government has decided to abolish it due to budgetary reasons. Aquatic institutions and schools across the country were shocked by the news and telegraphed to plead for its maintenance. The excerpts are as follows: (1) Song Junjian, Chairman of the Beiping Jicha Political Affairs Committee and Chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government, was shocked to learn that Hebei Province has decided to abolish the Provincial Aquatic College due to budgetary reasons. This school is the highest aquatic institution in the country, with a long history, complete equipment, and outstanding achievements. Once abolished, not only will students have nowhere to go, but aquatic professionals across the country will also lose their leadership. We hereby telegraphically request to maintain the status quo in order to value aquatic education. The Jiangsu Provincial Fisheries Experimental Farm, Wusong Aquatic School, Lianyungang Aquatic School, Zhejiang Provincial Aquatic Experimental Farm, Fujian Jimei Aquatic Navigation School, Guangdong Provincial Aquatic School, Shandong Provincial Aquatic Experimental Farm, and Shanghai Municipal Fisheries Guidance Office respectfully bow. The various institutions have expressed the same sentiments to the Beiping Jicha Political Affairs Committee and the Hebei Provincial Government.

Yangzhou Middle School in Jiangsu Province Establishes a Infant Cultivation Group

Yangzhou Middle School in Jiangsu Province has been promoting various scientific methods for handling household affairs since the establishment of the Women's Living Department, in order to create a standard for improving women's lives. The school regards infant cultivation as the most important responsibility in women's lives and as a kind of women's occupation. The school has specially added an infant cultivation park starting from this autumn, in order to promote scientific methods for cultivating infants, to provide opportunities for students in the Women's Living Department to practice, and to prepare for future employment. It is heard that the school has hired a doctor and two specialized pediatric nurses to be responsible for guidance and care. The daily work is carried out by students on a rotating basis. The school's charter is recorded below. Anyone who needs to foster children can contact the school's Living Department directly. The charter of the Yangzhou Middle School Women's Living Department Infant Meal Garden is as follows:

(1) Purpose: The purpose of this school is to cultivate healthy infants both physically and mentally. (2) Qualifications: This school only accepts normal infants aged one month to two years old without infectious diseases, and provides scientific cultivation, divided into two types: breast milk feeding and artificial milk feeding. (3) Quota: Six infants are currently scheduled. (4) Consignment period: This school temporarily provides day and night care for a period of three months. If you want to leave the school, please notify the school ten days before the end of the period, otherwise it will be considered as continuing to consign. (5) Payment: The consignment fee for infants is divided into two types: food and clothing, which are calculated and collected according to the value. (6) Admission Procedures: When an infant is admitted, the parents must fill out an application form and a guarantor must fill out a guarantee form and pay a deposit of ten yuan before the infant can be admitted to the school.

Academia Sinica Collects Bizarre Aquatic Products from the Yangtze River: Collectors Departed Yesterday

The National Academia Sinica has always attached great importance to the collection of various animal and plant specimens. Regarding aquatic products, researchers have been sent to various coastal areas and the Yangtze River basin to collect specimens, and have achieved considerable results. It is now learned that there are many bizarre aquatic products in the sea area from the north entrance of the Yangtze River to Haizhou that have not been discovered and studied by experts. Therefore, the Institute of Biology of the Academy has specially sent personnel to collect these bizarre aquatic products for reference. The collectors departed yesterday for a period of one month. It is hoped that they will achieve good results and provide materials for biological research.

Sports News

Reorganization Movement of the Shanghai Westerners' Football Club is in Full Swing: Mr. Davidson Plans to Fundamentally Reorganize the Westerners' Club, Whether the Junior Teams Support It is the Key to Success or Failure

The Shanghai Westerners' Football Club controls the authority of the Shanghai Sino-Western football scene. Its content and organization have never changed in the past 20 years. Whether it is the Shanghai A and B League, Cup matches, International Cup matches, or inter-port matches, they are all controlled by the club, which holds all the power. This is so-called monopolistic management. However, according to recent observations by football experts who have returned from England, this management and organizational content is outdated and does not conform to the trend. It should be immediately reorganized according to the British method to become a modern football club. The first person to propose this reorganization was a Scottish expert named Davidson. At last year's annual meeting of the Shanghai Westerners' Football Club, Davidson once proposed his reorganization plan, but the result was that Davidson failed. The Shanghai Westerners' Football Club still has the same organization and management. This year's annual meeting of the Westerners' Club is scheduled to be convened soon. After his failure last year, Davidson is preparing to make a second comeback this year. Such a big issue, which affects the entire Shanghai Sino-Western football scene, whether it will be established and passed in the future is worthy of attention from the sports community.

Davidson's Reorganization Plan

The most important content of Davidson's reorganization of the Shanghai Westerners' Football Club is to change the current monopolistic management system to a dual management system, that is, to separate the A and B Leagues from the Westerners' Football Club and make them independent, but under the supervision and command of the Westerners' Club. The football teams of the A League gather together to manage and hold the A League matches themselves. The B League is managed and held by the B League teams themselves. As for the Silver Cup, international matches, and inter-port matches, they will be handled by the Westerners' Club. In this way, the greatest benefit is to put the League and the Silver Cup in an equally important position. In the current state, it is common to see the Westerners' Club rush to finish the Silver Cup every year, and then hastily end the League. Under the club's own management, there will be no such situation. The second point is that players have an opportunity to appeal. In the current situation, players who are punished have nowhere to appeal. In the new system, players who are punished in the League can appeal to the Westerners' Football Club, the higher authority. These are the key points of Davidson's reorganization content.

The Key to Success or Failure Lies in the Junior Teams

Although this plan is a fatal blow to the current Shanghai Westerners' Football Club, because after the League becomes independent, the economic aspect will be severely hit. The biggest ticket revenue is in the League matches. Most of the senior teams agree with this plan because ticket revenue does not cause economic problems. However, junior teams have no hope of ticket revenue, so the key to the success or failure of this plan lies entirely in these junior teams. The failure of Davidson's plan last year was because the junior teams were wooed by the Westerners' Club and expressed their opposition. The success or failure this year still depends on their junior teams. However, it is heard that the Westerners' Club is also making arrangements. (Zhen)

The Whereabouts of Our Country's World Games Sports Delegation

Berlin Airmail: Our country's World Games sports delegation left Berlin on the 17th, arrived in Copenhagen, the capital of Denmark, on the 18th, left Denmark the next day, and arrived in Stockholm, the capital of Sweden, on the 19th. After visiting there, they left Stockholm the next day and returned to Berlin via Longter. They left Berlin on the 23rd and will arrive in Prague, the capital of the Czech Republic, the next day. On the 25th, they will arrive in Vienna, the capital of Austria, from Prague. On the 28th, they will arrive in Budapest, the capital of Hungary. It is expected that they will arrive in Rome on the 30th and Naples on September 3rd, and then set off to return home.
